Given a set of $n$ positive integers, $S = \\{ a_1, a_2, a_3, \\dots , a_n \\}$, and positive integer $W$, is there a subset of $S$ whose elements sum to $W$? A dynamic program for solving this problem uses a 2-dimensional Boolean array, $X$, with $n$ rows and $W+1$ columns.&nbsp;$X[i, j], 1 \\leq i \\leq n, 0 \\leq j \\leq&nbsp;W$, is TRUE, if and only if there is a subset of $\\{a_1, a_2, \\dots, a_i\\}$ whose elements sum to $j$.<\/p>\n\n<p>Which&nbsp;of the following is valid for $2 \\leq i \\leq n$, and $a_i \\leq j \\leq W$?<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>$X[i, j] = X[i-1, j] \\vee X[i, j-a_i]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[i, j] = X[i-1, j] \\vee&nbsp;X[i-1, j-a_i]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[i, j] = X[i-1, j] \\wedge X[i, j-a_i]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[i, j] = X[i-1, j] \\wedge&nbsp;X[i-1, j-a_i]$<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>The subset-sum problem is defined as follows. Given a set of $n$ positive integers, $S = \\{ a_1, a_2, a_3, \\dots , a_n \\}$, and positive integer $W$, is there a subset of $S$ whose elements sum to $W$? A dynamic program for solving this problem uses a 2-dimensional Boolean array, $X$, with $n$ rows and $W+1$ columns. $X[i, j], 1 \\leq i \\leq n, 0 \\leq j \\leq W$, is TRUE, if and only if there is a subset of $\\{a_1, a_2, \\dots, a_i\\}$ whose elements sum to $j$.<\/p>\n\n<p>Which entry of the array $X$, if TRUE, implies that there is a subset whose elements sum to $W$?<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>$X[1, W]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[n, 0]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[n, W]$<\/li>\n\t<li>$X[n-1, n]$<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>A sub-sequence of a given sequence is just the given sequence with some elements (possibly none or all) left out. We are given two sequences $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ of lengths $m$ and $n$, respectively with indexes of $X$ and $Y$ starting from $0$.<\/p>\n\n<p>We wish to find the length of the longest common sub-sequence (LCS) of $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ as $l(m, n)$, where an incomplete recursive definition for the function $I(i, j)$ to compute the length of the LCS of $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ is given below:<\/p>\n\n<pre class=\"text\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\nl(i,j)  = 0, if either i = 0 or j = 0\n        = expr1, if i,j &gt; 0 and X[i-1] = Y[j-1]\n        = expr2, if i,j &gt; 0 and X[i-1] \u2260 Y[j-1]\n<\/pre>\n\n<p>Which one of the following options is correct?<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>\n\t<p>$\\text{expr1} = l\\left(i-1, j\\right) +1$<\/p>\n\t<\/li>\n\t<li>\n\t<p>$\\text{expr1} = l\\left(i, j-1\\right)$<\/p>\n\t<\/li>\n\t<li>\n\t<p>$\\text{expr2} = \\max\\left(l\\left(i-1, j\\right), l\\left(i,j-1\\right)\\right)$<\/p>\n\t<\/li>\n\t<li>\n\t<p>$\\text{expr2} = \\max\\left(l\\left(i-1, j-1\\right), l\\left(i,j\\right)\\right)$<\/p>\n\t<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>A sub-sequence of a given sequence is just the given sequence with some elements (possibly none or all) left out. We are given two sequences $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ of lengths $m$ and $n$, respectively with indexes of $X$ and $Y$ starting from $0$.<\/p>\n\n<p>We wish to find the length of the longest common sub-sequence (LCS) of $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ as $l(m, n)$, where an incomplete recursive definition for the function $I(i, j)$ to compute the length of the LCS of $X[m]$ and $Y[n]$ is given below:<\/p>\n\n<p>$l(i,j) &nbsp;= 0$, if either $i = 0$ or $j = 0$<br>\n&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; $= expr1, if i,j &gt; 0 and X[i-1] = Y[j-1]$<br>\n&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; $= expr2, if i,j &gt; 0 and X[i-1] \u2260 Y[j-1]$<br>\nThe value of $l(i,j)$ could be obtained by dynamic programming based on the correct recursive definition of $l(i,j)$ of the form given above, using an array $L[M,N]$, where $M = m+1$ and $N = n+1$, such that $L[i, j] = l(i, j)$.<\/p>\n\n<p>Which one of the following statements would be TRUE regarding the dynamic programming solution for the recursive definition of $l(i, j)$?<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>All elements of $L$ should be initialized to 0 for the values of $l(i, j)$ to be properly computed.<\/li>\n\t<li>The values of $l(i, j)$ may be computed in a row major order or column major order of $L[M, N]$.<\/li>\n\t<li>The values of $l(i, j)$ cannot be computed in either row major order or column major order of $L[M, N]$.<\/li>\n\t<li>$L[p, q]$ needs to be computed before $L[r, s]$ if either $p&lt;r$ or $q &lt; s$.<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>The weight of a sequence $a_0,a_1, \\dots, a_{n-1}$ of real numbers is defined as $a_0+a_1\/2+ \\dots + a_{n-1}\/2^{n-1}$. A subsequence of a sequence is obtained by deleting some elements from the sequence, keeping the order of the remaining elements the same. Let $X$ denote the maximum possible weight of a subsequence of $a_o,a_1, \\dots, a_{n-1}$ and $Y$ the maximum possible weight of a subsequence of $a_1,a_2, \\dots, a_{n-1}$. Then $X$ is equal to<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>$max(Y, a_0+Y)$<\/li>\n\t<li>$max(Y, a_0+Y\/2)$<\/li>\n\t<li>$max(Y, a_0 +2Y)$<\/li>\n\t<li>$a_0+Y\/2$<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>An algorithm to find the length of the longest monotonically increasing sequence of numbers in an array $A[0:n-1]$ is given below.<\/p>\n\n<p>Let $L_i$, denote the length of the longest monotonically increasing sequence starting at index $i$ in the array.<\/p>\n\n<p>Initialize $L_{n-1} = 1$.<\/p>\n\n<p>For all $i$ such that $0 \\leq i \\leq n-2$<\/p>\n\n<p>$ L_i = \\begin{cases} 1+ L_{i+1} &amp; &nbsp;\\quad\\text{if A[i] &lt; A[i+1]} \\\\ 1 &amp; \\quad\\text{Otherwise}\\end{cases} $<\/p>\n\n<p>Finally the the length of the longest monotonically increasing sequence is $\\text{Max} \\:(L_0, L_1, \\dots , L_{n-1}).$<\/p>\n\n<p>Which of the following statements is&nbsp;<strong>TRUE<\/strong>?<\/p>\n\n<ol style=\"list-style-type:upper-alpha\">\n\t<li>The algorithm uses dynamic programming paradigm<\/li>\n\t<li>The algorithm has a linear complexity and uses branch and bound paradigm<\/li>\n\t<li>The algorithm has a non-linear polynomial complexity and uses branch and bound paradigm<\/li>\n\t<li>The algorithm uses divide and conquer paradigm<\/li>\n<\/ol>","<p>Four Matrices $M_1, M_2, M_3,$ and $M_4$ of dimensions $ p \\times q, \\:\\:q \\times r, \\:\\:r \\times s$ and $s \\times t$ respectively can be multiplied in several ways with different number of total scalar multiplications.
